<p>The <b>European Union</b> (<b>EU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Political_union" title="Political union">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_union" title="Economic union">economic union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">28 member states</a> that are located primarily in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. It has an area of 4,475,757&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,728,099&#160;sq&#160;mi), and an estimated population of over 510 million. The EU has developed <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">an internal single market</a> through a standardised system of laws that apply in all member states. EU policies aim to ensure the <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">free movement of people, goods, services, and capital</a> within the internal market,<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Internal_Market_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Internal_Market-16">[11]</a></sup> enact legislation in justice and home affairs, and maintain common policies on trade,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">fisheries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regional_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Regional policy of the European Union">regional development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[14]</a></sup> Within the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Passport_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Passport control">passport controls</a> have been abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-Internal_borders_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Internal_borders-20">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">A monetary union</a> was established in 1999 and came into full force in 2002, and is composed of <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">19 EU member states</a> which use the <a href="/wiki/Euro_currency" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro currency">euro currency</a>.</p>
<p>The EU operates through a hybrid system of <a href="/wiki/Supranational_union" title="Supranational union">supranational</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmental</a> decision-making.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-21">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-22">[17]</a></sup> The seven principal decision-making bodies—known as the <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institutions of the European Union</a>—are the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a>.</p>
<p>The EU traces its origins from the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC), formed by the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a> countries in 1951 and 1958, respectively. The community and its successors have grown in size by <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">the accession of new member states</a> and in power by the addition of policy areas to its remit. The <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> established the European Union in 1993 and introduced <a href="/wiki/European_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="European citizenship">European citizenship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115-23">[18]</a></sup> The latest major amendment to the constitutional basis of the EU, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>, came into force in 2009.</p>
<p>Covering 7.3% of the world population,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[19]</a></sup> the EU in 2016 generated a nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) of 16.477 trillion US dollars, constituting approximately 22.2% of global <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a> and 16.9% when measured in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[20]</a></sup> Additionally, 26 out of 28 EU countries have a very high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Programme</a>. In 2012, the EU was awarded the <a href="/wiki/2012_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2012 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[21]</a></sup> Through the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>, the EU has developed a role in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union" title="Foreign relations of the European Union">external relations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_European_Union" title="Military of the European Union">defence</a>. The union maintains permanent <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_European_Union" title="List of diplomatic missions of the European Union">diplomatic missions</a> throughout the world and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_United_Nations" title="European Union and the United Nations">represents itself</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_G7" title="European Union and the G7">G7</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/G-20" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20">G-20</a>. Because of its global influence, the European Union has been described as an <a href="/wiki/European_Union_as_an_emerging_superpower" title="European Union as an emerging superpower">emerging superpower</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_European_Superpower_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_European_Superpower-27">[22]</a></sup></p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Governance"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Governance</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Europe" title="History of Europe">History of Europe</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preliminary_.281945.E2.80.9357.29">Preliminary (1945–57)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_1" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:384px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_2&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/00/Schuman_Declaration.ogg/384px--Schuman_Declaration.ogg.jpg&quot; controls=&quot;&quot; preload=&quot;none&quot; autoplay=&quot;&quot; style=&quot;width:384px;height:288px&quot; class=&quot;kskin&quot; data-durationhint=&quot;27.92&quot; data-startoffset=&quot;0&quot; data-mwtitle=&quot;Schuman_Declaration.ogg&quot; data-mwprovider=&quot;local&quot;&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/00/Schuman_Declaration.ogg&quot; type=&quot;video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Original Ogg file, 384 × 288 (588 kbps)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;Ogg source&quot; data-width=&quot;384&quot; data-height=&quot;288&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;587607&quot; data-framerate=&quot;25&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/0/00/Schuman_Declaration.ogg/Schuman_Declaration.ogg.160p.ogv&quot; data-width=&quot;214&quot; data-height=&quot;160&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;195968&quot; data-framerate=&quot;15&quot;/&gt;&lt;track src=&quot;//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:Schuman_Declaration.ogg.en.srt&amp;amp;action=raw&amp;amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt&quot; data-dir=&quot;ltr&quot;/&gt;&lt;track src=&quot;//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:Schuman_Declaration.ogg.eu.srt&amp;amp;action=raw&amp;amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt&quot; kind=&quot;subtitles&quot; type=&quot;text/x-srt&quot; srclang=&quot;eu&quot; label=&quot;euskara (eu) subtitles&quot; data-mwtitle=&quot;TimedText:Schuman_Declaration.ogg.eu.srt&quot; data-mwprovider=&quot;local&quot; data-dir=&quot;ltr&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:Schuman Declaration.ogg" style="width:220px;height:165px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/00/Schuman_Declaration.ogg/220px-seek%3D23-Schuman_Declaration.ogg.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/00/Schuman_Declaration.ogg" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schuman_Declaration.ogg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a> <a href="/wiki/Schuman_Declaration" title="Schuman Declaration">proposing</a> the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">Coal and Steel Community</a> on <a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">9 May</a> 1950.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, European integration was seen as an antidote to the extreme nationalism which had devastated the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[23]</a></sup> The 1948 <a href="/wiki/Hague_Congress_(1948)" title="Hague Congress (1948)">Hague Congress</a> was a pivotal moment in European federal history, as it led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Movement_International" title="European Movement International">European Movement International</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Europe" title="College of Europe">College of Europe</a>, where Europe's future leaders would live and study together.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[24]</a></sup> 1952 saw the creation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, which was declared to be "a first step in the federation of Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[25]</a></sup> The supporters of the Community included <a href="/wiki/Alcide_De_Gasperi" title="Alcide De Gasperi">Alcide De Gasperi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Monnet" title="Jean Monnet">Jean Monnet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paul-Henri_Spaak" title="Paul-Henri Spaak">Paul-Henri Spaak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_History_45-59_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_45-59-31">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Rome_.281957.E2.80.9392.29">Treaty of Rome (1957–92)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/280px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" width="280" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/420px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/560px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The continental territories of the member states of the European Union (European Communities pre-1993), coloured in order of accession.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1957, Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a>, which created the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) and established a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">customs union</a>. They also signed another pact creating the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (Euratom) for co-operation in developing <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>. Both treaties came into force in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_History_45-59_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_45-59-31">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The EEC and Euratom were created separately from the ECSC, although they shared the same courts and the Common Assembly. The EEC was headed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Hallstein" title="Walter Hallstein">Walter Hallstein</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hallstein_Commission" title="Hallstein Commission">Hallstein Commission</a>) and Euratom was headed by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armand" title="Louis Armand">Louis Armand</a> (<a href="/wiki/Armand_Commission" title="Armand Commission">Armand Commission</a>) and then <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Hirsch" title="Étienne Hirsch">Étienne Hirsch</a>. Euratom was to integrate sectors in nuclear energy while the EEC would develop a customs union among members.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1960s, tensions began to show, with France seeking to limit supranational power. Nevertheless, in 1965 an agreement was reached and on 1 July 1967 the <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a> created a single set of institutions for the three communities, which were collectively referred to as the <i><a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_Merge_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Merge-34">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean_Rey_(politician)" title="Jean Rey (politician)">Jean Rey</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">presided over</a> the first merged Commission (<a href="/wiki/Rey_Commission" title="Rey Commission">Rey Commission</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG/220px-Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG/330px-Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG/440px-Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG 2x" data-file-width="661" data-file-height="498" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> fell, enabling the union to <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">expand</a> further (<a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> pictured).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1973, the Communities enlarged to include <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, which later <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_European_Economic_Community_membership_referendum,_1982" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenlandic European Economic Community membership referendum, 1982">left the Community</a> in 1985, following a dispute over fishing rights), <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_the_United_Kingdom_to_the_European_Communities" title="Accession of the United Kingdom to the European Communities">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_First_enlargement_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_First_enlargement-37">[32]</a></sup> Norway had negotiated to join at the same time, but Norwegian voters rejected membership in a <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1972" title="Norwegian European Communities membership referendum, 1972">referendum</a>. In 1979, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1979" title="European Parliament election, 1979">first direct elections</a> to the European Parliament were held.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_New_Parliament_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_New_Parliament-38">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> joined in 1981, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> following in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_Enlargement_negotiations_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Enlargement_negotiations-39">[34]</a></sup> In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> paved the way for the creation of open borders without passport controls between most member states and some non-member states.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[35]</a></sup> In 1986, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">European flag</a> began to be used by the Community<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[36]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a> was signed.</p>
<p>In 1990, after <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">the fall of the Eastern Bloc</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> became part of the Community as part of a <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunified Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_History_80-89_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_80-89-42">[37]</a></sup> With further enlargement planned to include the former <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist states</a> of Central and Eastern Europe, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a> for candidate members to join the EU were agreed upon in June 1993.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maastricht_Treaty_.281992.E2.80.932007.29">Maastricht Treaty (1992–2007)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Euro_banknotes_2002.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Euro_banknotes_2002.png/220px-Euro_banknotes_2002.png" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Euro_banknotes_2002.png/330px-Euro_banknotes_2002.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Euro_banknotes_2002.png/440px-Euro_banknotes_2002.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="587" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Euro_banknotes_2002.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> was introduced in 2002, replacing 12 national currencies. Seven countries have since joined.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The European Union was formally established when the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>—whose main architects were <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="François Mitterrand">François Mitterrand</a>—came into force on 1 November 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115-23">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[38]</a></sup> The treaty also gave the name <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a> to the EEC, even if it was referred as such before the treaty. In 1995, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> joined the EU.</p>
<p>In 2002, euro banknotes and coins replaced national currencies in 12 of the member states. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> has increased to encompass 19 countries. The euro currency became the second largest reserve currency in the world. In 2004, the EU saw <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">its biggest enlargement to date</a> when <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> joined the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_History_00_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_00-44">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lisbon_Treaty_.282007.E2.80.93present.29">Lisbon Treaty (2007–present)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> entered into force.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> became EU members. The same year, <a href="/wiki/Slovenian_euro_coins" title="Slovenian euro coins">Slovenia</a> adopted the euro,<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_History_00_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_00-44">[39]</a></sup> followed in 2008 by <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_euro_coins" title="Cypriot euro coins">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maltese_euro_coins" title="Maltese euro coins">Malta</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Slovak_euro_coins" title="Slovak euro coins">Slovakia</a> in 2009, by <a href="/wiki/Estonian_euro_coins" title="Estonian euro coins">Estonia</a> in 2011, by <a href="/wiki/Latvian_euro_coins" title="Latvian euro coins">Latvia</a> in 2014 and by <a href="/wiki/Lithuania_euro_coins" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuania euro coins">Lithuania</a> in 2015.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG/220px-Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG/330px-Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG/440px-Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Concert_2012_IMG_4451.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
EU representatives receive the Nobel Peace Prize in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 December 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> entered into force and reformed many aspects of the EU. In particular, it changed the legal structure of the European Union, merging the <a href="/wiki/Three_pillars_of_the_European_Union" title="Three pillars of the European Union">EU three pillars</a> system into a single legal entity provisioned with a <a href="/wiki/Legal_personality" title="Legal personality">legal personality</a>, created a permanent <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a>, the first of which was <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Herman Van Rompuy</a>, and strengthened the position of the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiris2010448_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiris2010448-45">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, the EU received the <a href="/wiki/2012_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2012 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for having "contributed to the advancement of peace and reconciliation, democracy, and human rights in Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[43]</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> became the 28th EU member.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the beginning of the 2010s, the cohesion of the European Union has been tested by several issues, including <a href="/wiki/European_debt_crisis" title="European debt crisis">a debt crisis in some of the Eurozone countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">increasing migration from the Middle East</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">United Kingdom's withdrawal from the EU</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCUKREFRESLT_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCUKREFRESLT-50">[45]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">referendum in the UK on its membership of the European Union</a> was held on 23 June 2016, with a majority of participants voting to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTEUBrexit_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEUBrexit-51">[46]</a></sup> As of December 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_Union&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the UK has not yet initiated the <a href="/wiki/Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">formal withdrawal procedure</a>, and will not leave the EU until two years after it notifies the European Council of its decision to withdraw, or until a withdrawal agreement comes into force.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCEUBrexit_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCEUBrexit-52">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_evolution">Structural evolution</span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_European_Union" title="Geography of the European Union">Geography of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:389px;max-width:389px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:210px;max-width:210px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:2rocks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Coast of Cyprus" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/2rocks.jpg/208px-2rocks.jpg" width="208" height="129" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/2rocks.jpg/312px-2rocks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/2rocks.jpg/416px-2rocks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3248" data-file-height="2016" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The 65,993&#160;km (41,006&#160;mi) coastline dominates the European climate (<a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>).</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:175px;max-width:175px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Mont Blanc" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG/173px-Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG" width="173" height="129" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG/260px-Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG/346px-Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> is the highest peak in the EU.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The EU's member states cover an area of 4,423,147 square kilometres (1,707,787&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Area.and.population.figure_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Area.and.population.figure-53">[f]</a></sup> The EU's highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Graian_Alps" title="Graian Alps">Graian Alps</a>, 4,810.45 metres (15,782&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[48]</a></sup> The lowest points in the EU are <a href="/wiki/Lammefjorden" title="Lammefjorden">Lammefjorden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zuidplaspolder" title="Zuidplaspolder">Zuidplaspolder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, at 7&#160;m (23&#160;ft) below sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[49]</a></sup> The landscape, climate, and economy of the EU are influenced by its coastline, which is 65,993 kilometres (41,006&#160;mi) long.</p>
<p>Including the overseas territories of France which are located outside the continent of Europe, but which are members of the union, the EU experiences most <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">types of climate</a> from <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">Arctic</a> (North-East Europe) to tropical (<a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>), rendering meteorological averages for the EU as a whole meaningless. The majority of the population lives in areas with a temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a> (North-Western Europe and Central Europe), a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (Southern Europe), or a warm summer continental or <a href="/wiki/Hemiboreal" title="Hemiboreal">hemiboreal</a> climate (Northern <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and Central Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-Humid_Continental_climate_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humid_Continental_climate-56">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The EU's population is highly urbanised, with some 75% of inhabitants living in <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> as of 2006. Cities are largely spread out across the EU, although with a <a href="/wiki/Blue_Banana" title="Blue Banana">large grouping</a> in and around the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[51]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states">Member states</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">Member state of the European Union</a></div>
<p>Through successive <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargements</a>, the European Union has grown from the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">six founding states</a>—Belgium, France, West Germany, Italy, Luxembourg, and the Netherlands—to the current 28. Countries accede to the union by becoming party to the founding <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>, thereby subjecting themselves to the privileges and obligations of EU membership. This entails a partial delegation of sovereignty to the institutions in return for representation within those institutions, a practice often referred to as "pooling of sovereignty".<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>To become a member, a country must meet the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a>, defined at the 1993 meeting of the European Council in Copenhagen. These require a stable democracy that respects human rights and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>; a functioning <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>; and the acceptance of the obligations of membership, including EU law. Evaluation of a country's fulfilment of the criteria is the responsibility of the European Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Accession_Criteria_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Accession_Criteria-60">[54]</a></sup> No member state has yet left the Union, although <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous area">autonomous province</a> of Denmark) withdrew in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> now contains a clause under Article 50, providing for a member to leave the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are six countries that are recognised as <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">candidates for membership</a>: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Albania_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Albania to the European Union">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Iceland_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Iceland to the European Union">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Macedonia to the European Union">Macedonia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[g]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">Serbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">Turkey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Enlargement_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Enlargement-64">[57]</a></sup> though Iceland suspended negotiations in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-icelandover_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icelandover-65">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Kosovo_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Kosovo to the European Union">Kosovo</a> are officially recognised as potential candidates,<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Enlargement_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Enlargement-64">[57]</a></sup> with Bosnia and Herzegovina having submitted a membership application.</p>
<p>The four countries forming the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> (EFTA) are not EU members, but have partly committed to the EU's economy and regulations: Iceland, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, which are a part of the <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a> through the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, which has similar ties through <a href="/wiki/Switzerland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Switzerland–European Union relations">bilateral treaties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EEA_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEA-66">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CH_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CH-67">[60]</a></sup> The relationships of the <a href="/wiki/Microstates_and_the_European_Union" title="Microstates and the European Union">European microstates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a> include the use of the euro and other areas of co-operation.<sup id="cite_ref-euro_use_world_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euro_use_world-68">[61]</a></sup> The following 28 <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a> (of which the map only shows territories situated in and around Europe) constitute the European Union:<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[62]</a></sup></p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_the_Environment" title="European Commissioner for the Environment">European Commissioner for the Environment</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Climate_Change_Programme" title="European Climate Change Programme">European Climate Change Programme</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg/220px-EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg/330px-EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg/440px-EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EE-Lahemaa-Bagno_Viru.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Viru Bog in <a href="/wiki/Lahemaa_National_Park" title="Lahemaa National Park">Lahemaa National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, a protected habitat under the <a href="/wiki/Habitats_Directive" title="Habitats Directive">Habitats Directive</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1957, when the EEC was founded, it had no environmental policy.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[63]</a></sup> Over the past 50 years, an increasingly dense network of legislation has been created, extending to all areas of environmental protection, including air pollution, water quality, waste management, nature conservation, and the control of chemicals, industrial hazards and biotechnology.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[64]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_European_Environmental_Policy" title="Institute for European Environmental Policy">Institute for European Environmental Policy</a>, environmental law comprises over 500 Directives, Regulations and Decisions, making environmental policy a core area of European politics.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-73">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>European policy-makers originally increased the EU's capacity to act on environmental issues by defining it as a trade problem.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trade_barrier" title="Trade barrier">Trade barriers</a> and competitive distortions in the Common Market could emerge due to the different environmental standards in each member state.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[67]</a></sup> In subsequent years, the environment became a formal policy area, with its own policy actors, principles and procedures. The legal basis for EU environmental policy was established with the introduction of the Single European Act in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-73">[65]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciconia_nigra_1_(Lukasz_Lukasik)_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ciconia_nigra_1_%28Lukasz_Lukasik%29_edit.jpg/220px-Ciconia_nigra_1_%28Lukasz_Lukasik%29_edit.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ciconia_nigra_1_%28Lukasz_Lukasik%29_edit.jpg/330px-Ciconia_nigra_1_%28Lukasz_Lukasik%29_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ciconia_nigra_1_%28Lukasz_Lukasik%29_edit.jpg/440px-Ciconia_nigra_1_%28Lukasz_Lukasik%29_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciconia_nigra_1_(Lukasz_Lukasik)_edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Black_stork" title="Black stork">black stork</a>, a protected species under Regulation (EC) No. 338/97</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Initially, EU environmental policy focused on Europe. More recently, the EU has demonstrated leadership in global environmental governance, e.g. the role of the EU in securing the ratification and coming into force of the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> despite opposition from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. This international dimension is reflected in the EU's Sixth Environmental Action Programme,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[68]</a></sup> which recognises that its objectives can only be achieved if key international agreements are actively supported and properly implemented both at EU level and worldwide. The Lisbon Treaty further strengthened the leadership ambitions.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[69]</a></sup> EU law has played a significant role in improving habitat and species protection in Europe, as well as contributing to improvements in air and water quality and waste management.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-73">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mitigating <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> is one of the top priorities of EU environmental policy. In 2007, member states agreed that, in future, 20% of the energy used across the EU must be <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable</a>, and carbon dioxide emissions have to be lower in 2020 by at least 20% compared to 1990 levels.<sup id="cite_ref-EUO_energy_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_energy-78">[70]</a></sup> The EU has adopted an <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">emissions trading system</a> to incorporate <a href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> into the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[71]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="European Green Capital">European Green Capital</a> is an annual award given to cities that focuses on the environment, energy efficiency and quality of life in urban areas to create <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart city</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Politics of the European Union">Politics of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The European Union operates according to the principles of <a href="/wiki/Principle_of_conferral" title="Principle of conferral">conferral</a> (which says that it should act only within the limits of the competences conferred on it by the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>) and of <a href="/wiki/Subsidiarity#European_Union_law" title="Subsidiarity">subsidiarity</a> (which says that it should act only where an objective cannot be sufficiently achieved by the member states acting alone). <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">Laws made by the EU institutions</a> are passed in a variety of forms. Generally speaking, they can be classified into two groups: those which come into force without the necessity for national implementation measures (regulations) and those which specifically require national implementation measures (directives).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_nature">Constitutional nature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">Treaties of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg/400px-Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg.png" width="400" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg/600px-Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg/800px-Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="721" data-file-height="506" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_System_of_the_European_Union.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Political system of the European Union</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The classification of the EU in terms of international or constitutional law has been much debated. It began life as an international organisation and gradually developed into a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a> of states. However, since the mid-1960s it has also added several of the key attributes of a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a>, such as the direct effect of the law of the general level of government upon the individual<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[73]</a></sup> and majority voting in the decision-making process of the general level of government,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[74]</a></sup> without becoming a federation <i>per se</i>. Scholars thus today see it as an intermediate form lying between a confederation and a federation, being an instance of neither political structure.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[75]</a></sup> For this reason, the organisation is termed <i><a href="/wiki/Sui_generis" title="Sui generis">sui generis</a></i> (incomparable, one of a kind),<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[76]</a></sup> although some argue that this designation is no longer valid.<sup id="cite_ref-Sch.C3.BCtze.2C_2012_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sch.C3.BCtze.2C_2012-85">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The organisation has traditionally used the terms "Community" and later "Union" to describe itself. The difficulties of classification involve the difference between national law (where the subjects of the law include natural persons and corporations) and <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> (where the subjects include sovereign states and international organisations). They can also be seen in the light of differing European and American constitutional traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Sch.C3.BCtze.2C_2012_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sch.C3.BCtze.2C_2012-85">[77]</a></sup> Especially in terms of the European tradition, the term federation is equated with a sovereign <a href="/wiki/Federal_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal state">federal state</a> in international law; so the EU cannot be called a federation — at least, not without qualification. It is, however, described as being based on a federal model or federal in nature; and so it may be appropriate to consider it a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal union of states</a>, a conceptual structure lying between the confederation of states and the federal state.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[79]</a></sup> The German Constitutional Court refers to the EU as a <i><a href="/wiki/Staatenverbund" title="Staatenverbund">Staatenverbund</a></i>, an intermediate structure between the <i>Staatenbund</i> (confederation of states) and the <i>Bundesstaat</i> (federal state), consistent with this concept.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[80]</a></sup> This may be a long-lived political form. Professor Andrew Moravcsik claims that the EU is unlikely to develop further into a federal state, but instead has reached maturity as a constitutional system.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">Institutions of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislature of the European Union">Legislature of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The European Union has seven institutions: the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a>. Competence in scrutinising and amending legislation is shared between the Council of the European Union and the European Parliament, while executive tasks are performed by the European Commission and in a limited capacity by the European Council (not to be confused with the aforementioned Council of the European Union). The <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> is determined by the European Central Bank. The interpretation and the application of EU law and the treaties are ensured by the Court of Justice of the European Union. The EU budget is scrutinised by the European Court of Auditors. There are also a number of ancillary bodies which advise the EU or operate in a specific area.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px">
<ul>
<li>summit of the <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of state">Heads of state</a> or <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of Government">government</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a>.</li>
<li>gives the necessary political impetus for the development of the Union and sets its general objectives and priorities</li>
<li>does not legislate</li>
<li>based in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px">
<ul>
<li>acts together with the Parliament as a <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a></li>
<li>shares with the Parliament the budgetary power</li>
<li>ensures coordination of the broad economic and social policy and sets out guidelines for the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a> (CFSP)</li>
<li>concludes <a href="/wiki/International_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="International agreement">international agreements</a></li>
<li>based in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px">
<ul>
<li>acts together with the Council as a <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a></li>
<li>shares with the Council the budgetary power and decides in the last instance on the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">budget</a></li>
<li>exerts the democratic control over the institutions including the European Commission and approves the Commission members</li>
<li>based in and plenary sessions in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, primarily meets in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px">
<ul>
<li>is the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a></li>
<li>submits proposals for new legislation to the Parliament and Council</li>
<li>implements policies</li>
<li>administers the <a href="/wiki/EU_budget" class="mw-redirect" title="EU budget">budget</a></li>
<li>ensures compliance with <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">European law</a> ("guardian of the treaties")</li>
<li>negotiates <a href="/wiki/International_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="International agreement">international agreements</a></li>
<li>based in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Council">European Council</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg/170px-Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg/255px-Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg/340px-Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1550" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The European Council gives political direction to the EU. It convenes at least four times a year and comprises the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a>), the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> and one representative per <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state</a> (either its <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> or <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>). The <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a>) also takes part in its meetings. It has been described by some as the Union's "supreme political authority".<sup id="cite_ref-How_work_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_work-91">[83]</a></sup> It is actively involved in the negotiation of <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaty changes</a> and defines the EU's policy agenda and strategies.</p>
<p>The European Council uses its leadership role to sort out disputes between member states and the institutions, and to resolve political crises and disagreements over controversial issues and policies. It acts externally as a "<a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">collective head of state</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratifies</a> important documents (for example, international agreements and treaties).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tasks for the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> are ensuring the external representation of the EU,<sup id="cite_ref-Council_Press_Release_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Press_Release-93">[85]</a></sup> driving consensus and resolving divergences among member states, both during meetings of the European Council and over the periods between them.</p>
<p>The European Council should not be mistaken for the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, an international organisation independent of the EU based in Strasbourg.</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_the_European_Union">Council of the European Union</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> (also called the "Council"<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[86]</a></sup> and the "Council of Ministers", its former title)<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[87]</a></sup> forms one half of the EU's legislature. It consists of a <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">government minister</a> from each member state and meets in <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union#Configurations" title="Council of the European Union">different compositions depending on the policy area being addressed</a>. Notwithstanding its different configurations, it is considered to be one single body.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Council_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Council-96">[88]</a></sup> In addition to its legislative functions, the Council also exercises <a href="/wiki/Executive_functions" title="Executive functions">executive functions</a> in relations to the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/220px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/330px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/440px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="3389" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Hemicycle" title="Hemicycle">hemicycle</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> in Strasbourg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> forms the other half of the <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislature of the European Union">EU's legislature</a>. The 751 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> (MEPs) are directly <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in the European Union">elected</a> by <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">EU citizens</a> every five years on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>. Although MEPs are elected on a national basis, they sit according to <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">political groups</a> rather than their nationality. Each country has a set number of seats and is divided into <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_constituency" title="European Parliament constituency">sub-national constituencies</a> where this does not affect the proportional nature of the voting system.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>The European Parliament and the Council of the European Union pass legislation jointly in nearly all areas under the <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">ordinary legislative procedure</a>. This also applies to the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EU budget</a>. The European Commission is accountable to Parliament, requiring its approval to take office, having to report back to it and subject to motions of censure from it. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tajani" title="Antonio Tajani">Antonio Tajani</a>) carries out the role of speaker in Parliament and represents it externally. The President and <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Vice President of the European Parliament">Vice-Presidents</a> are elected by MEPs every two and a half years.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Parliament_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Parliament-98">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Commission">European Commission</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg/170px-Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg/255px-Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg/340px-Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1225" data-file-height="1691" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">Commission President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> acts as the EU's <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive arm</a> and is responsible for <a href="/wiki/Right_of_initiative_(legislative)" title="Right of initiative (legislative)">initiating legislation</a> and the day-to-day running of the EU. The Commission is also seen as the motor of <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>. It operates as a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet government</a>, with 28 <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">Commissioners</a> for different areas of policy, one from each member state, though Commissioners are bound to represent the interests of the EU as a whole rather than their home state.</p>
<p>One of the 28 is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a>) appointed by the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>. After the President, the most prominent Commissioner is the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a>, who is <i>ex-officio</i> a <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_the_European_Commission" title="Vice-President of the European Commission">Vice-President of the Commission</a> and is also chosen by the European Council.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[91]</a></sup> The other 26 Commissioners are subsequently appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> in agreement with the nominated President. The 28 Commissioners as a single body are subject to a vote of approval by the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.</p>

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:silver; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Administration (6%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A49; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Citizenship, freedom, security and justice (1%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The EU had an agreed budget of €120.7&#160;billion for the year 2007 and €864.3&#160;billion for the period 2007–2013,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[93]</a></sup> representing 1.10% and 1.05% of the EU-27's <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> forecast for the respective periods. In 1960, the budget of the then European Economic Community was 0.03% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2010 budget of €141.5&#160;billion, the largest single expenditure item is "<i><a href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Fund" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Fund">cohesion &amp; competitiveness</a></i>" with around 45% of the total budget.<sup id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-103">[95]</a></sup> Next comes "<i><a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a></i>" with approximately 31% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-103">[95]</a></sup> "<i>Rural development, environment and <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">fisheries</a></i>" takes up around 11%.<sup id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-103">[95]</a></sup> "<i>Administration</i>" accounts for around 6%.<sup id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-103">[95]</a></sup> The "<i>EU as a global partner</i>" and "<i>citizenship, freedom, security and justice</i>" bring up the rear with approximately 6% and 1% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_103-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-103">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Auditors" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Auditors">Court of Auditors</a> is legally obliged to provide the Parliament and the Council with "a statement of assurance as to the reliability of the accounts and the legality and regularity of the underlying transactions".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[96]</a></sup> The Court also gives opinions and proposals on financial legislation and anti-fraud actions.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Auditors_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Auditors-105">[97]</a></sup> The Parliament uses this to decide whether to approve the Commission's handling of the budget.</p>
<p>The European Court of Auditors has signed off the European Union accounts every year since 2007<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> and, while making it clear that the European Commission has more work to do, has highlighted that most of the errors take place at national level.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Court_of_Auditors_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Court_of_Auditors-106">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-European_Commission_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Commission-107">[99]</a></sup> In their report on 2009 the auditors found that five areas of Union expenditure, <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Fund" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Fund">cohesion fund</a>, were materially affected by error.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[100]</a></sup> The European Commission estimated in 2009 that the financial effect of irregularities was €1,863&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competences">Competences</span></h3>
<p>EU member states retain all powers not explicitly handed to the European Union. In some areas the EU enjoys exclusive competence. These are areas in which member states have renounced any capacity to enact legislation. In other areas the EU and its member states share the competence to legislate. While both can legislate, member states can only legislate to the extent to which the EU has not. In other policy areas the EU can only co-ordinate, support and supplement member state action but cannot enact legislation with the aim of harmonising national laws.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>That a particular policy area falls into a certain category of competence is not necessarily indicative of what <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislature of the European Union">legislative procedure</a> is used for enacting legislation within that policy area. Different legislative procedures are used within the same category of competence, and even with the same policy area.</p>
<p>The distribution of competences in various policy areas between Member States and the Union is divided in the following three categories:</p>
