<p>Among the many languages and dialects used in the EU, it has 24 official and working languages: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Languages_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Languages-218">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[196]</a></sup> Important documents, such as legislation, are translated into every official language.</p>
<p>The European Parliament provides translation into all languages for documents and its plenary sessions.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[197]</a></sup> Some institutions use only a handful of languages as internal working languages.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[198]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> are not official languages of the EU but have semi-official status in that official translations of the treaties are made into them and citizens of the EU have the right to correspond with the institutions using them.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Language_policy" title="Language policy">Language policy</a> is the responsibility of member states, but EU institutions promote the learning of other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[x]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[199]</a></sup> English is the most widely spoken language in the EU, being spoken by 51% of the EU population when counting both native and non-native speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_P4_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages_P4-224">[200]</a></sup> German is the most widely spoken mother tongue, being spoken by 16% of the EU population. 56% of EU citizens are able to engage in a conversation in a language other than their mother tongue.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_P3_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages_P3-225">[201]</a></sup> Most official languages of the EU belong to the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language family</a>, except Estonian, Finnish, and Hungarian, which belong to the <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic</a> language family, and Maltese, which is a <a href="/wiki/Semitic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Semitic language">Semitic language</a>. Most EU official languages are written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> except Bulgarian, which is written in the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillic alphabet">Cyrillic alphabet</a>, and Greek, which is written in the <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">Greek alphabet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Many_tongues.2C_one_family_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Many_tongues.2C_one_family-226">[202]</a></sup> These are the three official scripts of the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides the 24 official languages, there are about 150 <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">regional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">minority languages</a>, spoken by up to 50&#160;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-Many_tongues.2C_one_family_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Many_tongues.2C_one_family-226">[202]</a></sup> Although EU programmes can support regional and minority languages, the protection of <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_rights" title="Linguistic rights">linguistic rights</a> is a matter for the individual member states. The <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a> ratified by most EU states provides general guidelines that states can follow to protect their linguistic heritage.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Day_of_Languages" title="European Day of Languages">European Day of Languages</a> is held annually on 26 September and is aimed at encouraging language learning across Europe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_European_Union" title="Religion in the European Union">Religion in the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden">

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Self described religion in the European Union (2012)<sup id="cite_ref-euroreligion2012_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euroreligion2012-5">[3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> (48%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:SkyBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> (12%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox</a> (8%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:teal; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian (4%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non believer/Agnostic (16%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">Atheist</a> (7%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> (2%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:LightGrey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religion/None stated (3%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The EU has no formal connection to any religion. The <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Consolidated_version_of_the_Treaty_on_the_Functioning_of_the_European_Union/Part_One:_Principles#Article_17" class="extiw" title="s:Consolidated version of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union/Part One: Principles">Article 17 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a> recognises the "status under national law of churches and religious associations" as well as that of "philosophical and non-confessional organisations".<sup id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaties_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaties-228">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>The preamble to the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Treaty on European Union</a> mentions the "cultural, religious and humanist inheritance of Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaties_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaties-228">[204]</a></sup> Discussion over the draft texts of the European Constitution and later the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> included proposals to mention <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> or <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>, or both, in the preamble of the text, but the idea faced opposition and was dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-EUO_Merkel_God_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_Merkel_God-229">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>Christians in the EU are divided among members of Catholicism (both <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Rite</a>), numerous <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> denominations (<a href="/wiki/Anglicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> forming the bulk of this category), and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>. In 2009, the EU had an estimated <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Muslim_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Muslim population">Muslim population</a> of 13&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-mgmpPRC_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgmpPRC-230">[206]</a></sup> and an estimated <a href="/wiki/Jewish_population" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish population">Jewish population</a> of over a million.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[207]</a></sup> The other world religions of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> are also represented in the EU population.</p>
<p>According to new polls about religiosity in the European Union in 2012 by <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the largest religion in the European Union, accounting for 72% of the EU population.<sup id="cite_ref-euroreligion2012_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euroreligion2012-5">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> group, accounting for 48% of the EU population, while <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestants</a> make up 12%, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> make up 8% and other Christians make up 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> opinion polls showed in 2005 that 52% of EU citizens believed in a God, 27% in "some sort of spirit or life force", and 18% had no form of belief.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-233">[209]</a></sup> Many countries have experienced falling church attendance and membership in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-About_SecE_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_SecE-234">[210]</a></sup> The countries where the fewest people reported a religious belief were Estonia (16%) and the Czech Republic (19%).<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-233">[209]</a></sup> The most religious countries were Malta (95%, predominantly Roman Catholic) as well as Cyprus and Romania (both predominantly Orthodox) each with about 90% of citizens professing a belief in God. Across the EU, belief was higher among women, older people, those with religious upbringing, those who left school at 15 or 16 and those "positioning themselves on the right of the political scale".<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_233-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-233">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Educational_policies_and_initiatives_of_the_European_Union" title="Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union">Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erasmus_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Erasmus_logo.svg/170px-Erasmus_logo.svg.png" width="170" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Erasmus_logo.svg/255px-Erasmus_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Erasmus_logo.svg/340px-Erasmus_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="258" data-file-height="308" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erasmus_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus Programme</a> logo, representing the European student exchange</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Basic education is an area where the EU's role is limited to supporting national governments. In higher education, the policy was developed in the 1980s in programmes supporting exchanges and mobility. The most visible of these has been the <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus Programme</a>, a university exchange programme which began in 1987. In its first 20&#160;years, it has supported international exchange opportunities for well over 1.5&#160;million university and college students and has become a symbol of European student life.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are now similar programmes for school pupils and teachers, for trainees in <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education and training</a>, and for adult learners in the <a href="/wiki/Lifelong_Learning_Programme_2007%E2%80%932013" title="Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013">Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013</a>. These programmes are designed to encourage a wider knowledge of other countries and to spread good practices in the education and training fields across the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[213]</a></sup> Through its support of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a>, the EU is supporting comparable standards and compatible degrees across Europe.</p>
<p>Scientific development is facilitated through the EU's <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">Framework Programmes</a>, the first of which started in 1984. The aims of EU policy in this area are to co-ordinate and stimulate research. The independent <a href="/wiki/European_Research_Council" title="European Research Council">European Research Council</a> allocates EU funds to European or national research projects.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[214]</a></sup> EU <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">research and technological framework programmes</a> deal in a number of areas, for example energy where the aim is to develop a diverse mix of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> to help the environment and to reduce dependence on imported fuels.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Europe" title="Healthcare in Europe">Healthcare in Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg/220px-Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg/330px-Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg/440px-Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="626" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a><br />
(French version pictured)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although the EU has no major competences in the field of health care, Article 35 of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a> affirms that "A high level of human health protection shall be ensured in the definition and implementation of all Union policies and activities". The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Health_and_Consumers_(European_Commission)" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorate-General for Health and Consumers (European Commission)">Directorate-General for Health and Consumers</a> seeks to align national laws on the protection of people's health, on the consumers' rights, on the safety of food and other products.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>All EU and many other European countries offer their citizens a free <a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a> which, on a reciprocal basis, provides insurance for emergency medical treatment insurance when visiting other participating European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[219]</a></sup> A directive on cross-border healthcare aims at promoting co-operation on health care between member states and facilitating access to safe and high-quality cross-border healthcare for European patients.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[222]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">Culture of Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Cultural policies of the European Union">Cultural policies of the European Union</a></div>
<p>Cultural co-operation between member states has been a concern of the EU since its inclusion as a community competency in the Maastricht Treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-Bozoki_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bozoki-247">[223]</a></sup> Actions taken in the cultural area by the EU include the <a href="/wiki/Culture_2000" title="Culture 2000">Culture 2000</a> seven-year programme,<sup id="cite_ref-Bozoki_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bozoki-247">[223]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/European_Cultural_Month" title="European Cultural Month">European Cultural Month</a> event,<sup id="cite_ref-Culture_Month_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culture_Month-248">[224]</a></sup> and orchestras such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Youth_Orchestra" title="European Union Youth Orchestra">European Union Youth Orchestra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> programme selects one or more cities in every year to assist the <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">cultural development</a> of that city.<sup id="cite_ref-Capital_Culture_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capital_Culture-250">[226]</a></sup> 53 EU cities have been part of this initiative up to 2016.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Sport policies of the European Union">Sport policies of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Europe" title="Sport in Europe">Sport in Europe</a></div>
<p>Sport is mainly the responsibility of the member states or other international organisations, rather than of the EU. However, there are some EU policies that have affected sport, such as the free movement of workers, which was at the core of the <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman ruling</a> that prohibited national football leagues from imposing quotas on foreign players with European citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Boseman_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Boseman-251">[227]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> requires any application of economic rules to take into account the specific nature of sport and its structures based on voluntary activity.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[228]</a></sup> This followed lobbying by governing organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, due to objections over the application of free market principles to sport, which led to an increasing gap between rich and poor clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_RT_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_RT-253">[229]</a></sup> The EU does fund a programme for Israeli, Jordanian, Irish, and British football coaches, as part of the Football 4 Peace project.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[230]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Symbols_of_Europe" title="Symbols of Europe">Symbols of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg/170px-1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg/255px-1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg/340px-1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1_May_2004_enlargement_celebration_in_Parc_du_Cinquantenaire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">European flag</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">2004 enlargement</a> celebrations</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">flag of the Union</a> consists of a <a href="/wiki/Circle_of_stars" title="Circle of stars">circle of</a> 12 golden stars on a blue background. The blue represents the West, while the number and position of the stars represent completeness and unity, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-36th_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36th-255">[231]</a></sup> Originally designed in 1955 for the Council of Europe, the flag was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a>, the predecessors of the present Union, in 1986.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Motto_of_the_European_Union" title="Motto of the European Union">United in Diversity</a></i> was adopted as the motto of the Union in the year 2000, having been selected from <a href="/wiki/A_motto_for_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="A motto for Europe">proposals</a> submitted by school pupils.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimons2002110_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimons2002110-256">[232]</a></sup> Since 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag day">flag day</a> of the Union has been <a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">Europe Day</a>, on 9 May (the date of the 1950 <a href="/wiki/Schuman_declaration" class="mw-redirect" title="Schuman declaration">Schuman declaration</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Anthem_of_Europe" title="Anthem of Europe">anthem of the Union</a> is an instrumental version of the prelude to the <i><a href="/wiki/Ode_to_Joy" title="Ode to Joy">Ode to Joy</a></i>, the 4th movement of <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Beethoven)">ninth symphony</a>. The anthem was adopted by European Community leaders in 1985 and has since been played on official occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[233]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raptus_Europae.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Raptus_Europae.png/220px-Raptus_Europae.png" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/Raptus_Europae.png 1.5x" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="204" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raptus_Europae.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a> and the bull, depicted in <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_et_accurata_totius_Europ%C3%A6_descriptio.jpg" title="File:Nova et accurata totius Europæ descriptio.jpg">a 1700 map</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides naming the continent, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythological</a> figure of <a href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a> has frequently been employed as a <a href="/wiki/National_personification" title="National personification">personification</a> of Europe. Known from the myth in which <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> seduces her in the guise of a white bull, Europa has also been referred to in relation to the present Union. Statues of Europa and the bull decorate several of the Union's institutions and a portrait of her is seen on the 2013 series of <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">Euro banknotes</a>. The bull is, for its part, depicted on all residence permit cards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDemey2007387_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDemey2007387-258">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charles the Great</a>, also known as Charlemagne (<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la"><i>Carolus Magnus</i></span>) and later recognised as <i>Pater Europae</i> ("Father of Europe"),<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-259">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[239]</a></sup> has a symbolic relevance to Europe. The Commission has named <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_building" title="Charlemagne building">one of its central buildings</a> in Brussels after Charlemagne and the city of <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> has since 1949 awarded the <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_Prize" title="Charlemagne Prize">Charlemagne Prize</a> to champions of European unification.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[240]</a></sup> Since 2008, the organisers of this prize, in conjunction with the European Parliament, have awarded the <a href="/wiki/European_Charlemagne_Youth_Prize" title="European Charlemagne Youth Prize">Charlemagne Youth Prize</a> in recognition of similar efforts by young people.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[241]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Benedict_of_Nursia" title="Benedict of Nursia">Benedict of Nursia</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 2 March 480 – 543 or 547 AD) is a <a href="/wiki/Patron_saints_of_Europe" title="Patron saints of Europe">patron saint of Europe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SHMI_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SHMI-266">[242]</a></sup> venerated in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Churches</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodox Churches</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Catholic_Church" title="Old Catholic Church">Old Catholic Churches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Barry1995_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barry1995-267">[243]</a></sup> Pope <a href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> said that he "exercised a fundamental influence on the development of European civilization and culture" and helped Europe to emerge from the "dark night of history" that followed the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman empire">Roman empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[244]</a></sup> The influence of St Benedict produced "a true spiritual ferment" in Europe, his followers spreading his <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_Saint_Benedict" title="Rule of Saint Benedict">Rule</a> across the continent to establish a new cultural unity based on Christian faith.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[245]</a></sup> In 1997, Polish-born <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> canonised <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>'s 14th-century monarch <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Jadwiga</a> as Saint Hedwig, the <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of queens and of European unification<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[246]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_freedom_in_the_European_Union" title="Media freedom in the European Union">Media freedom in the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Europe" title="Cinema of Europe">Cinema of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MEDIA_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/73/MEDIA_logo.svg/210px-MEDIA_logo.svg.png" width="210" height="53" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/73/MEDIA_logo.svg/315px-MEDIA_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/73/MEDIA_logo.svg/420px-MEDIA_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="642" data-file-height="162" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MEDIA_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo of the EU MEDIA Programme</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Media_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Media freedom">Media freedom</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_rights" title="Fundamental rights">fundamental right</a> that applies to all <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a> of the European Union and its <a href="/wiki/EU_citizens" class="mw-redirect" title="EU citizens">citizens</a>, as defined in the <a href="/wiki/EU_Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="EU Charter of Fundamental Rights">EU Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eprs_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eprs-271">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1</sup> Within the <a href="/wiki/EU_enlargement" class="mw-redirect" title="EU enlargement">EU enlargement</a> process, guaranteeing media freedom is named a "key indicator of a country's readiness to become part of the EU".<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/MEDIA_Programme" title="MEDIA Programme">MEDIA Programme</a> of the European Union intends to support the European popular film and audiovisual industries since 1991. It provides support for the development, promotion and distribution of European works within Europe and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[249]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-189"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-189">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although almost all uranium is imported, nuclear power is considered primary energy produced in the EU.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Court of Justice of the European Union, Judgement of 5 February 1963 in Case 26/62, 'Van Gend en Loos', <i>European Court Reports 1963</i>, p. 1.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Single European Act, Article 100a, Approximation of Laws.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, David Marquand says it is ‘less than a federation but more than a confederation’; Brigid Laffan and Kimmo Kiljunen both see it residing ‘between a confederation and a federation’; Thomas Hueglin and Alan Fenna locate it ‘somewhere between federation and confederation’; and Kalypso Nicolaidis argues ‘it is more than a confederation of sovereign states; ... (however, it) should not become a federal state’.<br />
Michael Burgess enlarges: the EU 'is not a federation but it is also more than a confederation understood in the classical sense. It exists, then, in a kind of conceptual limbo, a twilight zone ... which has no name'.<br />
Paul Magnette illuminates the nature of the perceived 'in-betweenness': 'Since the seventeenth century, legal theorists have repeated that only two forms of union between states are possible: either the confederation, born of an international treaty concluded between sovereign states, where all decisions are unanimously adopted by state representatives; or the federal state, established by a constitution, where the law voted on by a bicameral parliament applies directly to the citizens. <i>Tertium non datur</i>. There is no third way ... In these, classic, political terms, the European Union is, strictly speaking, inconceivable'.<br />
Burgess, Michael (2000) <i>Federalism and European Union: The Building of Europe 1950–2000</i>, Routledge, London, pp. 41–2. Hueglin, Thomas and Fenna, Alan (2006) <i>Comparative Federalism: A Systematic Inquiry</i>, Broadview, Peterborough, p. 13. Kiljunen, Kimmo (2004) <i>The European Constitution in the Making</i>, Centre for European Policy Studies, Brussels, p. 22. Laffan, Brigid (2002) <i>The Future of Europe Debate</i>, Institute of European Affairs, Dublin, p. 10. Magnette, Paul (2005) <i>What Is the European Union? Nature and Prospects</i>, Palgrave Macmillan, Basingstoke, pp. 4–5, 190. Marquand, David (2006) ‘Federalism and the British: Anatomy of a Neurosis’, in <i>Political Quarterly</i>, Vol. 77, No. 2, p. 175. Nicolaidis, Kalypso (2004) ‘We, the Peoples of Europe ...’, in <i>Foreign Affairs</i>, Vol. 83, No. 6, pp. 101–2.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jacques Delors, the President of the European Commission upon entry into force of the Single European Act, which introduced the widespread use of majority voting to complete the single market, saw it as having at that stage become an ‘Unidentified Political Object’. Speech at the People's University, Lille, 8 March 1987.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/geos/ee.html">"Is Europe still sui generis? Signals from The White Paper on European Governance"</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 February</span> 2016</span>. <q>...&#160;we see the notions of governance deployed in the White Paper as undermining the description of the EU as sui generis. It is becoming like a national state, but we differ from many of the critics (or enthusiasts) of the White Paper in one major way. Rather than seeing the EU becoming a state-like object, taking on the trappings of a 19th—or more correctly 20th—century state, we see national states moving towards the EU, adopting many of the governing practices advocated by the White Paper.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEuropean+Union&amp;rft.btitle=Is+Europe+still+sui+generis%3F+Signals+from+The+White+Paper+on+European+Governance&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.cia.gov%2Flibrary%2Fpublications%2Fthe-world-factbook%2Fgeos%2Fee.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For the derivation of this concept, see the Introduction of the entry on <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">Federalism</a>.<br />
Law, John (2013) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.on-federalism.eu/attachments/169_download.pdf">"How Can We Define Federalism?"</a>. <i>Perspectives on Federalism</i>, Vol. 5, No. 3, p. E104.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20121022061516/http://www.bundesverfassungsgericht.de/en/press/bvg09-072en.html">"Federal Constitutional Court Press Release No. 72/2009 of 30 June 2009. Judgment of 30 June 2009: Act Approving the Treaty of Lisbon compatible with the Basic Law; accompanying law unconstitutional to the extent that legislative bodies have not been accorded sufficient rights of participation"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bundesverfassungsgericht.de/en/press/bvg09-072en.html">the original</a> on 22 October 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">17 November</span> 2012</span>. <q>Due to this structural democratic deficit, which cannot be resolved in an association of sovereign national states (<i>Staatenverbund</i>), further steps of integration that go beyond the status quo may undermine neither the States' political power of action nor the principle of conferral. The peoples of the Member States are the holders of the constituent power. The Basic Law does not permit the special bodies of the legislative, executive and judicial power to dispose of the essential elements of the constitution, i.e. of the constitutional identity (Article 23.1 sentence 3, Article 79.3 GG). The constitutional identity is an inalienable element of the democratic self-determination of a people.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEuropean+Union&amp;rft.btitle=Federal+Constitutional+Court+Press+Release+No.+72%2F2009+of+30+June+2009.+Judgment+of+30+June+2009%3A+Act+Approving+the+Treaty+of+Lisbon+compatible+with+the+Basic+Law%3B+accompanying+law+unconstitutional+to+the+extent+that+legislative+bodies+have+not+been+accorded+sufficient+rights+of+participation&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bundesverfassungsgericht.de%2Fen%2Fpress%2Fbvg09-072en.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Moravcsik, Andrew; Moravcsik, Andrew (2009) [2004]. <li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/news/article.cfm?c_id=2&amp;objectid=10685127">"Britain and France to work together"</a> by Catherine Field. 4 November 2010. nzherald.co.nz. According to the Stockholm International Peace Research Institute (SIPRI), Britain spent more than US$69 billion on defence last year, placing it third in the world after the United States and China, while France spent US$67.31 billion, the fourth largest. Together, Britain and France account for 45 per cent of Europe's defence budget, 50 per cent of its military capacity and 70 per cent of all spending in military research and development. Copyright 2010, APN Holdings NZ Limited.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-EurostatEnergy-190"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-EurostatEnergy_190-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EurostatEnergy_190-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation pressrelease"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://epp.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/pls/portal/docs/PAGE/PGP_PRD_CAT_PREREL/PGE_CAT_PREREL_YEAR_2008/PGE_CAT_PREREL_YEAR_2008_MONTH_07/8-10072008-EN-AP.PDF">"Energy consumption and production: EU27 energy dependence rate at 54% in 2006: Energy consumption stable"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span> (Press release). Eurostat. 10 July 2008<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 September</span> 2008</span>. <q><br />
In the EU27, gross inland energy consumption was 1 825&#160;million tonnes of oil equivalent (toe) in 2006, stable compared with 2005, while energy production decreased by 2.3% to 871 mn toe&#160;...<br />
Gross inland consumption is defined as primary production plus imports, recovered products and stock change, less exports and fuel supply to maritime bunkers (for seagoing ships of all flags)&#160;...<br />
A tonne of oil equivalent (toe) is a standardised unit defined on the basis of one tonne of oil having a net calorific value of 41.868 Gigajoules.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEuropean+Union&amp;rft.btitle=Energy+consumption+and+production%3A+EU27+energy+dependence+rate+at+54%25+in+2006%3A+Energy+consumption+stable&amp;rft.date=2008-07-10&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fepp.eurostat.ec.europa.eu%2Fpls%2Fportal%2Fdocs%2FPAGE%2FPGP_PRD_CAT_PREREL%2FPGE_CAT_PREREL_YEAR_2008%2FPGE_CAT_PREREL_YEAR_2008_MONTH_07%2F8-10072008-EN-AP.PDF&amp;rft.pub=Eurostat&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Euratom2007-191"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Euratom2007_191-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Euratom2007_191-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">"EU supply and demand for nuclear fuels". <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/euratom/ar/last.pdf"><i>Euratom Supply Agency—Annual Report 2007</i></a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. Luxembourg: Office for Official Publications of the European Communities. 2008. p.&#160;22. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-92-79-09437-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-92-79-09437-8">978-92-79-09437-8</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">1 March</span> 2009</span>. <q>European uranium mining supplied just below 3% of the total EU needs, coming from the Czech Republic and Romania (a total of 526 tU).</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEuropean+Union&amp;rft.atitle=EU+supply+and+demand+for+nuclear+fuels&amp;rft.btitle=Euratom+Supply+Agency%94Annual+Report+2007&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fec.europa.eu%2Feuratom%2Far%2Flast.pdf&amp;rft.isbn=978-92-79-09437-8&amp;rft.pages=22&amp;rft.place=Luxembourg&amp;rft.pub=Office+for+Official+Publications+of+the+European+Communities&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span><br />
Nuclear energy and renewable energy are treated differently from oil, gas , and coal in this respect.</span></li>

<li><span style="font-size:90%;">1998</span> <a href="/wiki/John_Hume" title="John Hume">John Hume</a>&#160;/ <a href="/wiki/David_Trimble" title="David Trimble">David Trimble</a></li>
<li><span style="font-size:90%;">1999</span> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="Médecins Sans Frontières">Médecins Sans Frontières</a></li>
<li><span style="font-size:90%;">2000</span> <a href="/wiki/Kim_Dae-jung" title="Kim Dae-jung">Kim Dae-jung</a></li>
